P. J. Bowler, [3mLifeโs Splendid Drama [0m(Chicago University Press, 1996): a historical account of the efforts of scientists to 
reconstruct the history of life on earth. 

R. M. Henig, [3mThe Monk in the Garden [0m(Houghton Mifflin, 2000): describes Gregor Mendelโs plant-breeding xperiments, and deals with 
how Mendelโs work was rediscovered. 

E. Mayr, [3mWhat Evolution Is [0m(Basic Books, 2001): a good introduction to the principles of, and evidence for, evolution. 

J. A. Moore, [3mSience as a Way of Knowing [0m(Harvard University Press, 1993): beginning with the Greeks it traces the history of the 
major developments in biological research. 

M. Pagel, [3mEncyclopedia of Evolution [0m(Oxford University Press, 2002): contains detailed articles about the main elements of 
evolutionary science. 

M. Ridley, [3mEvolution [0m(Blackwell, 2003): includes both evolutionary theory and the evidence for evolution. 

[1mุงููุตู ุงูุซุงูุซ [0m

J. Kalb, [3mAdventures in the Bone Trade: The Race to Discover Human Ancestors in Ethiopiaโs Afar Depression [0m(Springer-Verlag, 2001): 
focuses on the competition among scientific teams searching for early hominin fossils. 

V. Morrell, [3mAncestral Passions [0m(Simon & Schuster, 1996): describes the Leakey family and many of their important discoveries. 

P. [3mShipman, The Man Who Found the Missing Link: Eugene Dubois and his Lifelong Quest to Prove Darwin Right [0m(Simon & Schuster, 
2001): describes the efforts made by Eugรจne Dubois to find fossil hominins in Java. 

C. S. Swisher III, G. H. Curtis, and Roger Lewin, [3mJava Man: How Two Geologistsโ Dramatic Discoveries Changed our Understanding of 
the Evolutionary Path to Modern Humans [0m(Scribner, 2000): chronicles efforts to generate absolute dates for the Javan hominins. 

[1mูู ุงููุตู ุงูุฑุงุจุน ุฅูู ุงููุตู ุงูุณุงุฏุณ [0m

E. Delson, I. Tattersall, J. van Couvering, and A. Brooks, [3mEncyclopedia of Human Evolution and Prehistory [0m(Garland, 2000): 
detailed entries for nearly all the fossils and hominin species included in these and later chapters. 

J. K. McKee, [3mThe Riddled Chain: Chance, Coincidence, and Chaos in Human Evolution [0m(Rutgers University Press, 2000): argues that 
the evidence linking events in hominin evolution with changing climates is weak. 

R. Potts, [3mHumanityโs Descent: The Consequences of Ecological Instability [0m(Avon, 1997): argues that much of human evolution is a 
response to an increasingly unstable climate. 

C. Stringer and P. Andrews, [3mThe Complete World of Human Evolution [0m(Thames & Hudson, 2005): an excellent up-to-date account of the 
hominin fossil evidence and the methods used to interpret it. 

I. Tattersall, [3mThe Fossil Trail: How we Know What we Think we Know about Human Evolution [0m(Oxford University Press, 1995): a very 
readable account of the history of the discovery and interpretation of the hominin fossil record. 

I. Tattersall and J. H. Schwartz, [3mExtinct Humans [0m(Westview Press, 2000): excellent illustrations of the hominin fossil record. 

[1mุงููุตู ุงูุณุงุจุน [0m

J. L. Arsuaga, [3mThe Neanderthalโs Necklace: In Search of the First Thinkers [0m(Four Walls Eight Windows, 2001): the leader of the

J. L. Arsuaga and I. Martinez, [3mThe Chosen Species: The Long March of Human Evolution [0m(Blackwell, 2005): an up-to-date summary of 
human evolution that concentrates on the later part of the hominin fossil record.
